## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical kinetics
**Analysis**: This task belongs to chemical kinetics because the target variable dA_dt is the instantaneous rate of change of concentration A, and the features are time t and concentration A, which are the fundamental variables in differential rate laws.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order decay: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, e.g., surface-saturated catalyst or photochemical reaction with constant light intensity)
- First-order decay: dA_dt = c0 * A (unimolecular irreversible reaction, exponential decay)
- Second-order single reactant: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (bimolecular reaction of A with itself, or two identical molecules)
- Second-order two reactants with fixed stoichiometry: dA_dt = c0 * A * (A + c1) (A reacting with another species whose concentration is linearly related to A)
- nth-order decay: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (power-law dependence, phenomenological order)
- Reversible first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A - c1 * (c2 - A) (opposing unimolecular reactions, equilibrium approach)
- Autocatalytic: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (self-catalysis, logistic-type growth, product accelerates reaction)
- Mixed-order saturation: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A) (Langmuir–Hinshelwood or enzyme-like saturation when A is adsorbed or bound)
- Substrate inhibition: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + c2 * A + A**2) (rate decrease at high concentration due to inhibition)
- Consecutive first-order source-sink: dA_dt = c0 * (c1 - A) - c2 * A (formation from precursor and decay in series)
- Time-dependent rate constant: dA_dt = c0 * t**c1 * A (reaction rate varying with time, e.g., non-isothermal or catalyst deactivation)
- Polynomial rate law: dA_dt = c0 + c1 * A + c2 * A**2 + c3 * A**3 (empirical global rate expression for complex mechanisms)
- Fractional order: dA_dt = c0 * (A + c1)**c2 (shifted power law, approximate intermediate kinetics)
- Exponential decay in concentration: dA_dt = c0 * exp(c1 * A) (rare, e.g., high-order phenomenological fit)
- Product-inhibited first order: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + c2 * (c3 - A)) (product accumulation reduces effective rate)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Reaction order → Power-law term with exponent on A (dA_dt ∝ A^n) indicates molecularity or empirical order
- Reversibility → Rate expression contains both positive and negative terms (e.g., loss and gain of A), often linear combinations of A and (C – A)
- Autocatalysis → Product of A and (C – A) terms produces sigmoidal concentration-time curve and rate maximum at intermediate conversion
- Saturation kinetics → Rational form A/(K+A) describes rate reaching a plateau when active sites or catalysts are fully occupied
- Inhibition → Rational denominator with higher powers of A (e.g., 1 + a*A + b*A^2) suppresses rate at high A, a signature of substrate or product inhibition
- Parallel pathways → Sum of independent rate contributions, often a sum of simple monomials with different orders
- Consecutive reactions → Rate of A includes both a formation term (from precursor) and a decay term, leading to a difference of two rate laws
- Time-dependence of rate constant → Explicit appearance of t outside A, such as t^n * A, indicating catalyst aging or external parameter drift
- Empirical complex kinetics → Polynomial or rational approximations with several terms are used when the mechanism involves multiple elementary steps and intermediates
- Observed half-life scaling → For a power-law rate dA/dt = -k A^n, the half-life depends on initial concentration as A0^(1-n), providing a diagnostic for order n
